### Post by okkie2 on 2015-04-22
Hope you all having a nice day.
I have a new Samsung phone and need to transfer photos etc to my computer, Bluetooth and everything else unsuccessful. Is there a way I can get software somewhere for my computer to solve the problem?

---

### Post by decrepit on 2015-04-22
Older versions of Ubuntu, don't work with modern android phones. I have 14.04 installed, and I can connect with my Samsung Ace3 via USB, full access to internal memory and the SD card.
But you need the latest MTP software.

Don't know about blue tooth this PC doesn't have it.

---

### Post by cbraxton on 2015-04-22
I have had success using QtADB and AAFM to transfer files from Samsung phones via USB. (These are graphical front-ends to the adb command-line program.)

### Post by okkie2 on 2015-04-28
So back to my samsung problem.
Since I have been trying to get my phone connected, I noticed the following when I do an update: W: Failed to fetch cdrom://Ubuntu 14.04.1 LTS _Trusty Tahr_ - Release amd64 (20140722.2)/dists/trusty/restricted/binary-i386/Packages  Please use apt-cdrom to make this CD-ROM recognized by APT. apt-get update cannot be used to add new CD-R
Could this have anything to do with my trying to have the phone connected to the computer? I only have one cd rom and an external drive.could the computer see the phone as a cd rom. Stupid question but needs to be asked before I continue. Thanks

---

### Post by decrepit on 2015-04-29
Looks like apt is trying to update from the installation CD. You need to set it to the local mirror server, then you'll be able to install the MTP software you need to talk to your phone.

### Post by Bucky Ball on 2015-05-10
Just throwing this in, but does the phone need to be set to act as an MTP device and not a phone (set on the phone, not the computer)? Some devices do. When you plug it in, what comes up on the screen of the phone? Does it give an option to toggle to MTP?

---

### Post by okkie2 on 2015-05-11
like I said, if I plug the phone into the USB socket I can see the phone in the sidebar but not open it.once connected , the only option I can find on the phone itself is USB tethering and when activated the phone symbol in the sidebar is gone and nothing on the computer screen either. no reaction from the phone either when plugged in.
Thanks

---

### Post by decrepit on 2015-05-11
Okie yes you are on the right track, but Bucky Ball has a very good point. My Galaxy Ace3 has two modes of talking to the PC, MTP and PTP. Once the phone is plugged into the computer if you tap on the USB connection on the phones screen, it should give you the choice between the 2 modes.
PTP is mainly for photos, MTP is for media.
USB tethering is for using the phone as an internet modem for the computer, not what you want at all.

---

### Post by efflandt on 2015-05-17
Which Ubuntu version do you have. I never could get MTP to work properly in 12.04 (Samsung S3), it would show root directories of internal storage & microSD, but nothing under that. The earliest version I tried that MTP just worked automatically was Ubuntu 13.10 (no longer supported). In Ubuntu 14.04 MTP it also simply worked with the default file manager without having to do add anything.

If all else fails install **AndFTP** app on your phone and **ssh** package on your PC if you do not already have openssh-server (by default only ssh client is installed, ssh meta package makes sure you also have ssh server). Then if your phone is connected to local WiFi you should be able to use AndFTP to sftp from your phone to Ubuntu. Or **SSHServer** app on your phone would allow you to do same in other direction (sftp or ssh to your phone). And as a side note **ConnectBot** is an Android ssh client (but you may need to set its font larger). I used those apps in 12.04 when MTP did not work.

The format for your phone already in /lib/udev/rules.d/**69-libmtp.rules** of 14.04 (based on vender and product IDs you entered above) is:```
# Samsung Galaxy Y
ATTR{idVendor}=="04e8", ATTR{idProduct}=="685e", SYMLINK+="libmtp-%k", MODE="660", GROUP="audio", ENV{ID_MTP_DEVICE}="1", ENV{ID_MEDIA_PLAYER}="1"
```But if you are trying to get MTP working in Ubuntu 12.04 or older, good luck, I never could.

### Post by coffeecat on 2015-05-18
Use the advanced message editor. Click on the "manage attachments" button below the text editor. In the new mini-window, click on Add files, then on the browse button and select your image. Now click on upload and your selected image will appear in the attachments pane, pre-ticked. Click on Insert Inline. Your image will appear as a thumbnail.
